<td colspan="2" style="padding-left:0;">These are the titles as given in the <i>Constitution of the Republic of Cameroon</i>, Article X (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060228030033/http://confinder.richmond.edu/admin/docs/Cameroon.pdf">English</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> (archived February 28, 2006) and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060228030033/http://www.prc.cm/instit/consti.htm">French</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> (archived February 28, 2006) versions). 18 January 1996. The French version of the song is sometimes called <span lang="fr"><i>Chant de Ralliement</i></span>, as in Swarovski Orchestra (2004). <i>National Anthems of the World</i>. Koch International Classics; and the English version "O Cameroon, Cradle of Our Forefathers", as in <a href="#DeLancey">DeLancey and DeLancey</a> 61.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Cameroon</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˌ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">æ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'m' in 'my'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">m</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ə</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'r' in 'rye'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">r</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/uː/ long 'oo' in 'food'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">uː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>, officially the <b>Republic of Cameroon</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>République du Cameroun</i></span>), (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>Republik Kamerun</i></span>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to the west; <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to the northeast; the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the east; and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the south. Cameroon's coastline lies on the <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Bonny" title="Bight of Bonny">Bight of Bonny</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the Atlantic Ocean. The country is often referred to as "Africa in miniature" for its geological and cultural diversity. Natural features include beaches, deserts, mountains, rainforests, and savannas. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a> in the southwest, and the largest cities are <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Garoua" title="Garoua">Garoua</a>. Cameroon is home to over 200 different linguistic groups. The country is well known for its native styles of music, particularly <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bikutsi" title="Bikutsi">bikutsi</a>, and for its successful <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national football team</a>. French and English are the official languages. After independence, the newly united nation joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, although the vast majority of its territories had previously been a German colony and, after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, a French mandate.</p>
<p>Early inhabitants of the territory included the <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao civilisation</a> around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baka_(Cameroon_and_Gabon)" title="Baka (Cameroon and Gabon)" class="mw-redirect">Baka</a> hunter-gatherers in the southeastern rainforest. <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese explorers</a> reached the coast in the 15th century and named the area <i>Rio dos Camarões</i> (<i>Shrimp River</i>), which became <i>Cameroon</i> in English. <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> soldiers founded the <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Emirate" title="Adamawa Emirate">Adamawa Emirate</a> in the north in the 19th century, and various ethnic groups of the west and northwest established powerful chiefdoms and <a href="/wiki/Fon_(Cameroon)" title="Fon (Cameroon)" class="mw-redirect">fondoms</a>. Cameroon became a <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German colony</a> in 1884 known as Kamerun.</p>
<p>After World War I, the territory was divided between <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union des Populations du Cameroun</a> (UPC) political party advocated independence, but was outlawed by France in the 1950s. It waged war on French and UPC militant forces until 1971. In 1960, the French-administered part of Cameroon became independent as the Republic of Cameroun under President <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">southern part</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a> merged with it in 1961 to form the <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">Federal Republic</a> of Cameroon. The country was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">United Republic</a> of Cameroon in 1972 and the Republic of Cameroon in 1984.</p>
<p>Cameroon enjoys relatively high political and social stability. This has permitted the development of agriculture, roads, railways, and large petroleum and timber industries. Nevertheless, large numbers of Cameroonians live in poverty as subsistence farmers. Power lies firmly in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a> president since 1982, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a>, and his <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_People%27s_Democratic_Movement" title="Cameroon People's Democratic Movement">Cameroon People's Democratic Movement</a> party. The English-speaking territories of Cameroon have grown increasingly alienated from the government, and politicians from those regions have called for greater decentralization and even secession (for example: the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons_National_Council" title="Southern Cameroons National Council">Southern Cameroons National Council</a>) of the former British-governed territories.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cameroon" title="History of Cameroon">History of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shumom-text.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg/220px-Shumom-text.jpg" width="220" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg/330px-Shumom-text.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg 2x" data-file-width="371" data-file-height="478" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shumom-text.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bamum_script" title="Bamum script">Bamum script</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The territory of present day Cameroon was first settled during the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> Era. The longest continuous inhabitants are groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Baka_(Cameroon_and_Gabon)" title="Baka (Cameroon and Gabon)" class="mw-redirect">Baka</a> (Pygmies).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> From here, <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu migrations</a> into eastern, southern, and central Africa are believed to have originated about 2,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-history_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao</a> culture arose around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> c. AD 500 and gave way to the <a href="/wiki/Kanem_Empire" title="Kanem Empire">Kanem</a> and its successor state, the <a href="/wiki/Bornu_Empire" title="Bornu Empire">Bornu Empire</a>. Kingdoms, <a href="/wiki/Fon_(Cameroon)" title="Fon (Cameroon)" class="mw-redirect">fondoms</a>, and chiefdoms arose in the west.<sup id="cite_ref-Njung_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Njung-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese sailors</a> reached the coast in 1472. They noted an abundance of the ghost shrimp <i><a href="/wiki/Lepidophthalmus_turneranus" title="Lepidophthalmus turneranus">Lepidophthalmus turneranus</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Wouri_River" title="Wouri River">Wouri River</a> and named it <span lang="pt"><i>Rio dos Camarões</i></span> (<i>Shrimp River</i>), which became <i>Cameroon</i> in English.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Over the following few centuries, European interests regularised trade with the coastal peoples, and Christian <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> pushed inland.<sup id="cite_ref-Fanso_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fanso-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Modibo_Adama" title="Modibo Adama">Modibo Adama</a> led <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> soldiers on a <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a> in the north against non-Muslim and partially Muslim peoples and established the <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Emirate" title="Adamawa Emirate">Adamawa Emirate</a>. Settled peoples who fled the Fulani caused a major redistribution of population.<sup id="cite_ref-Fanso_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fanso-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The northern part of Cameroon was an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-history_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Bamum people have an indigenous writing system, known as <a href="/wiki/Bamum_script" title="Bamum script">Bamum script</a> or Shu Mom. The script was developed by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Njoya" title="Ibrahim Njoya">Ibrahim Njoya</a> in 1896,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NMAA_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMAA-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and is taught in Cameroon by the <a href="/wiki/Bamum_Scripts_and_Archives_Project" title="Bamum Scripts and Archives Project">Bamum Scripts and Archives Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NMAA_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMAA-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> claimed the territory as the colony of <a href="/wiki/Kamerun" title="Kamerun">Kamerun</a> in 1884 and began a steady push inland. They initiated projects to improve the colony's infrastructure, relying on a harsh system of <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">forced labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_125_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_125-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With the defeat of Germany in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Kamerun became a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> territory and was split into <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">French</a> <span lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/Cameroun" title="Cameroun">Cameroun</a></span> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Cameroons" title="Cameroons" class="mw-redirect">Cameroons</a> in 1919. France integrated the economy of Cameroun with that of France<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_5_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_5-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and improved the infrastructure with capital investments, skilled workers, and continued forced labour.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_125_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_125-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The British administered their territory from neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. Natives complained that this made them a neglected "colony of a colony". Nigerian migrant workers flocked to Southern Cameroons, ending forced labour but angering indigenous peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The League of Nations mandates were converted into <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">United Nations Trusteeships</a> in 1946, and the question of independence became a pressing issue in French Cameroun.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_5_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_5-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>France outlawed the most radical political party, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union des Populations du Cameroun</a> (UPC), on 13 July 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> This prompted a long guerrilla war and the assassination of the party's leader, <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Um_Nyob%C3%A9" title="Ruben Um Nyobé">Ruben Um Nyobé</a>. In British Cameroons, the question was whether to reunify with French Cameroun or join Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281960.29">Independence (1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Independence (1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:166px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg" width="164" height="211" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="164" data-file-height="211" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former president <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a> ruled from 1960 until 1982.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 January 1960 French Cameroun gained independence from France under President <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a>. On 1 October 1961, the formerly British <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">Southern Cameroons</a> united with French Cameroun to form the Federal Republic of Cameroon. Ahidjo used the ongoing war with the UPC to concentrate power in the presidency, continuing with this even after the suppression of the UPC in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_6_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_6-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>His political party, the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_National_Union" title="Cameroon National Union" class="mw-redirect">Cameroon National Union</a> (CNU), became the sole legal political party on 1 September 1966 and in 1972, the <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal system of government</a> was abolished in favour of a United Republic of Cameroon, headed from <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Ahidjo pursued an economic policy of <a href="/wiki/Planned_liberalism" title="Planned liberalism">planned liberalism</a>, prioritising <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" title="Cash crops" class="mw-redirect">cash crops</a> and petroleum exploitation. The government used oil money to create a national cash reserve, pay farmers, and finance major development projects; however, many initiatives failed when Ahidjo appointed unqualified allies to direct them.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_2014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/220px-Paul_Biya_2014.png" width="220" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/330px-Paul_Biya_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/440px-Paul_Biya_2014.png 2x" data-file-width="517" data-file-height="617" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_2014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul Biya has ruled the country since 1982</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ahidjo stepped down on 4 November 1982 and left power to his constitutional successor, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a>. However, Ahidjo remained in control of the CNU and tried to run the country from behind the scenes until Biya and his allies pressured him into resigning. Biya began his administration by moving toward a more democratic government, but a failed <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Palace_Guard_Revolt" title="Cameroonian Palace Guard Revolt" class="mw-redirect">coup d'état</a> nudged him toward the leadership style of his predecessor.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Economic_crisis_of_Cameroon" title="Economic crisis of Cameroon">economic crisis</a> took effect in the mid-1980s to late 1990s as a result of international economic conditions, drought, falling petroleum prices, and years of corruption, mismanagement, and <a href="/wiki/Cronyism" title="Cronyism">cronyism</a>. Cameroon turned to foreign aid, cut government spending, and <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatised</a> industries. With the reintroduction of multi-party politics in December 1990, the former British Cameroons pressure groups called for greater autonomy, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons_National_Council" title="Southern Cameroons National Council">Southern Cameroons National Council</a> advocated complete secession as the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Ambazonia" title="Ambazonia">Ambazonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_9_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_9-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2008, Cameroon experienced its worst violence in 15 years when a transport union strike in Douala escalated into <a href="/wiki/2008_Cameroonian_anti-government_protests" title="2008 Cameroonian anti-government protests">violent protests</a> in 31 municipal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Nkemngu_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nkemngu-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Matthews_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matthews-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Chibok_schoolgirl_kidnapping" title="Chibok schoolgirl kidnapping" class="mw-redirect">Chibok schoolgirl kidnapping</a>, Presidents Paul Biya of Cameroon and Idriss Deby of Chad announced they are waging war on <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram" title="Boko Haram">Boko Haram</a>, and deployed troops to the Nigerian border.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YaoundeUnityPalace.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/300px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png" width="300" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/450px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/600px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png 2x" data-file-width="605" data-file-height="399" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YaoundeUnityPalace.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Unity Palace – Cameroon Presidency.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cameroon" title="Politics of Cameroon">Politics of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_Cameroon" title="Heads of state of Cameroon" class="mw-redirect">President of Cameroon</a> is elected and has refers to the assembly to create policy, administer government agencies, command the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Cameroon" title="Military of Cameroon" class="mw-redirect">armed forces</a>, negotiate and ratify treaties, and declare a state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_250_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The president appoints government officials at all levels, from the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cameroon" title="Prime Minister of Cameroon">prime minister</a> (considered the official head of government), to the provincial governors and divisional officers.<sup id="cite_ref-msu_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msu-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The president is selected by popular vote every seven years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Cameroon" title="National Assembly of Cameroon" class="mw-redirect">National Assembly</a> makes legislation. The body consists of 180 members who are elected for five-year terms and meet three times per year.<sup id="cite_ref-msu_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msu-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Laws are passed on a majority vote. Rarely has the assembly changed or blocked legislation proposed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 1996 constitution establishes a second house of parliament, the 100-seat Senate, was established in April 2013 and is headed by a senate president who is the constitutional successor in case of untimely vacancy of the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The government recognises the authority of traditional chiefs, fons, and <a href="/wiki/Lamido" title="Lamido">lamibe</a> to govern at the local level and to resolve disputes as long as such rulings do not conflict with national law.<sup id="cite_ref-State_Dept_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameroon's legal system is largely based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French civil law</a> with common law influences.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Although nominally independent, the judiciary falls under the authority of the executive's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_of_Cameroon" title="Ministry of Justice of Cameroon">Ministry of Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-State_Dept_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The president appoints judges at all levels.<sup id="cite_ref-msu_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msu-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The judiciary is officially divided into tribunals, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_Cameroon" title="Court of Appeal of Cameroon">court of appeal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Cameroon" title="Supreme Court of Cameroon">supreme court</a>. The National Assembly elects the members of a nine-member <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice_(Cameroon)" title="High Court of Justice (Cameroon)">High Court of Justice</a> that judges high-ranking members of government in the event they are charged with high treason or harming national security.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cameroon is viewed as rife with corruption at all levels of government. In 1997, Cameroon established anti-corruption bureaus in 29 ministries, but only 25% became operational,<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and in 2012, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> placed Cameroon at number 144 on a list of 176 countries ranked from least to most corrupt.<sup id="cite_ref-Corruption_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corruption-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> On 18 January 2006, Biya initiated an anti-corruption drive under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/National_Anti-Corruption_Observatory" title="National Anti-Corruption Observatory">National Anti-Corruption Observatory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> There are several high corruption risk areas in Cameroon, for instance, customs, public health sector and public procurement.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/170px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/255px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/340px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A statue of a chief in <a href="/wiki/Bana,_Cameroon" title="Bana, Cameroon">Bana</a>, West Region.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Human rights organisations accuse police and military forces of mistreating and even torturing criminal suspects, ethnic minorities, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Cameroon" title="LGBT rights in Cameroon">homosexuals</a>, and political activists.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EHRC_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHRC-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Prisons are overcrowded with little access to adequate food and medical facilities,<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EHRC_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHRC-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> and prisons run by traditional rulers in the north are charged with holding political opponents at the behest of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> However, since the first decade of the 21st century, an increasing number of police and gendarmes have been prosecuted for improper conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>President Biya's <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_People%27s_Democratic_Movement" title="Cameroon People's Democratic Movement">Cameroon People's Democratic Movement</a> (CPDM) was the only legal political party until December 1990. Numerous regional political groups have since formed. The primary opposition is the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Front_(Cameroon)" title="Social Democratic Front (Cameroon)">Social Democratic Front</a> (SDF), based largely in the Anglophone region of the country and headed by <a href="/wiki/John_Fru_Ndi" title="John Fru Ndi">John Fru Ndi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lergai_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lergai-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Biya and his party have maintained control of the presidency and the National Assembly in national elections, which rivals contend were unfair.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLancey_9_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_9-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Human rights organisations allege that the government suppresses the freedoms of opposition groups by preventing demonstrations, disrupting meetings, and arresting opposition leaders and journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> ranks Cameroon as "not free" in terms of political rights and civil liberties.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The last <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_parliamentary_election,_2007" title="Cameroonian parliamentary election, 2007">parliamentary elections</a> were held on 22 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Kandemeh_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kandemeh-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cameroon" title="Foreign relations of Cameroon">Foreign relations of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>Cameroon is a member of both the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" title="Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">La Francophonie</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cameroon" title="Foreign relations of Cameroon">foreign policy</a> closely follows that of its main ally, France (the former colonial ruler).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameroon relies heavily on France for its defence,<sup id="cite_ref-State_Dept_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> although military spending is high in comparison to other sectors of government.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Biya has clashed with the government of Nigeria over possession of the oil rich <a href="/wiki/Bakassi" title="Bakassi">Bakassi</a> peninsula (however, this was resolved with <a href="/wiki/Greentree_Agreement" title="Greentree Agreement">Greentree Agreement</a>) and with <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>'s president, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Bongo" title="Omar Bongo">El Hadj Omar Bongo</a>, over personal rivalries.<sup id="cite_ref-lergai_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lergai-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Cameroon" title="Regions of Cameroon">Regions of Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Cameroon" title="Departments of Cameroon">Departments of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/170px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/255px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/340px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="586" data-file-height="769" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cameroon is divided into 10 regions.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Cameroon" title="Constitution of Cameroon">constitution</a> divides Cameroon into 10 semi-autonomous regions, each under the administration of an elected <a href="/wiki/Regional_Council_(Cameroon)" title="Regional Council (Cameroon)">Regional Council</a>. Each region is headed by a presidentially appointed governor.<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_250_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>These leaders are charged with implementing the will of the president, reporting on the general mood and conditions of the regions, administering the civil service, keeping the peace, and overseeing the heads of the smaller administrative units. Governors have broad powers: they may order propaganda in their area and call in the army, <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmes</a>, and police.<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_250_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> All local government officials are employees of the central government's Ministry of Territorial Administration, from which local governments also get most of their budgets.<sup id="cite_ref-history_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The regions are subdivided into 58 divisions (French <span lang="fr"><i>départements</i></span>). These are headed by presidentially appointed divisional officers (<span lang="fr"><i><a href="/wiki/Prefect" title="Prefect">préfets</a></i></span>). The divisions are further split into sub-divisions (<span lang="fr"><i>arrondissements</i></span>), headed by assistant divisional officers (<span lang="fr"><i>sous-prefets</i></span>). The districts, administered by district heads (<span lang="fr"><i>chefs de district</i></span>), are the smallest administrative units.<sup id="cite_ref-unhchr_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhchr-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The three northernmost regions are the <a href="/wiki/Far_North_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Far North Region (Cameroon)">Far North</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Extrême Nord</i></span>), <a href="/wiki/North_Region_(Cameroon)" title="North Region (Cameroon)">North</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Nord</i></span>), and <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Region" title="Adamawa Region">Adamawa</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Adamaoua</i></span>). Directly south of them are the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Centre Region (Cameroon)">Centre</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Centre</i></span>) and <a href="/wiki/East_Region_(Cameroon)" title="East Region (Cameroon)">East</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Est</i></span>). The <a href="/wiki/South_Region_(Cameroon)" title="South Region (Cameroon)">South Province</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Sud</i></span>) lies on the Gulf of Guinea and the southern border. Cameroon's western region is split into four smaller regions: the <a href="/wiki/Littoral_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Littoral Region (Cameroon)">Littoral</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Littoral</i></span>) and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Sud-Ouest</i></span>) regions are on the coast, and the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Northwest Region (Cameroon)">Northwest</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Nord-Ouest</i></span>) and <a href="/wiki/West_Region_(Cameroon)" title="West Region (Cameroon)">West</a> (<span lang="fr"><i>Ouest</i></span>) regions are in the western grassfields.<sup id="cite_ref-unhchr_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhchr-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_health">Education and health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Education and health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Cameroon" title="Education in Cameroon">Education in Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Cameroon" title="Health in Cameroon">Health in Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid,_center,_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala,_Cameroon,_March_19,_2014,_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/450px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/600px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid,_center,_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala,_Cameroon,_March_19,_2014,_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
School children in Cameroon.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate of Cameroon was estimated to be 71.3% (male 78.3% and female 64.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Most children have access to state-run schools that are cheaper than private and religious facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The educational system is a mixture of British and French precedents<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> with most instruction in English or French.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameroon has one of the highest school attendance rates in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Girls attend school less regularly than boys do because of cultural attitudes, domestic duties, early marriage and pregnancy, and sexual harassment. Although attendance rates are higher in the south,<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> a disproportionate number of teachers are stationed there, leaving northern schools chronically understaffed.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>School attendance in Cameroon is also affected by <a href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor" class="mw-redirect">child labor</a>. In fact, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" title="U.S. Department of Labor" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Labor</a> Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor reported that 56% of children aged 5 to 14 were working children and that almost 53% of children aged 7 to 14 combined work and school.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2014, a <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i> issued by the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_International_Labor_Affairs" title="Bureau of International Labor Affairs">Bureau of International Labor Affairs</a> mentioned Cameroon among the countries that resorted to child labor in the production of cocoa.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The quality of health care is generally low.<sup id="cite_ref-yqheor_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yqheor-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In Cameroon, there is only one doctor for every 5,000 people, according to the World Health Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to financial cuts in the health care system there are few professionals. Doctors and nurses, which were trained in Cameroon, emigrate because in Cameroon the payment is bad for too much work. Nurses are unemployed even though their help is needed. Some of them even help out voluntarily so they will not lose their skills.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Outside the major cities, facilities are often dirty and poorly equipped.<sup id="cite_ref-West_64_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_64-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Life expectancy at birth is estimated to be 54.71 years in 2012, among the lowest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Endemic diseases include <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">filariasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leishmaniasis" title="Leishmaniasis">leishmaniasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schistosomiasis" title="Schistosomiasis">schistosomiasis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>/<a href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS" class="mw-redirect">AIDS</a> seroprevalence rate is estimated at 5.4% for those aged 15–49,<sup id="cite_ref-UNAIDS_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNAIDS-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> although a strong stigma against the illness keeps the number of reported cases artificially low.<sup id="cite_ref-yqheor_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yqheor-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Breast_ironing" title="Breast ironing">Breast ironing</a>, a traditional practice that is prevalent in Cameroon, may affect girls' health.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM), while not widespread, is practiced among some populations; according to a 2013 UNICEF report,<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> 1% of women in Cameroon have undergone FGM. <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">Traditional healers</a> remain a popular alternative to Western medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-Lantum_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lantum-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cameroon" title="Geography of Cameroon">Geography of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/220px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/330px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/440px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Volcanic_plugs" title="Volcanic plugs" class="mw-redirect">Volcanic plugs</a> dot the landscape near <a href="/wiki/Rhumsiki" title="Rhumsiki">Rhumsiki</a>, Far North Region.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 475,442 square kilometres (183,569&#160;sq&#160;mi), Cameroon is the world's 53rd-largest country.<sup id="cite_ref-Demographic_Yearbook_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demographic_Yearbook-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> It is slightly larger than the nation of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>. The country is located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central</a> and West Africa on the <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Bonny" title="Bight of Bonny">Bight of Bonny</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameroon lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/1st_parallel_north" title="1st parallel north">1°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/8th_meridian_east" title="8th meridian east">8°</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_meridian_east" title="17th meridian east">17°E</a>.</p>
<p>Tourist literature describes Cameroon as "Africa in miniature" because it exhibits all major climates and vegetation of the continent: coast, desert, mountains, rainforest, and savanna.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The country's neighbours are Nigeria to the west; <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to the northeast; the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the east; and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, Gabon and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameroon is divided into five major geographic zones distinguished by dominant physical, climatic, and vegetative features. The coastal plain extends 15 to 150 kilometres (9 to 93&#160;mi) inland from the Gulf of Guinea<sup id="cite_ref-Fomensky_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fomensky-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> and has an average elevation of 90 metres (295&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Exceedingly hot and humid with a short <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, this belt is densely forested and includes some of the <a href="/wiki/Debundscha" title="Debundscha">wettest places</a> on earth, part of the <a href="/wiki/Cross-Sanaga-Bioko_coastal_forests" title="Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests">Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Extremes_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Extremes-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_Cameroon_Plateau" title="South Cameroon Plateau">South Cameroon Plateau</a> rises from the coastal plain to an average elevation of 650 metres (2,133&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_16_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_16-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Equatorial rainforest dominates this region, although its alternation between <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet</a> and dry seasons makes it is less humid than the coast. This area is part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Equatorial_coastal_forests" title="Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests">Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/220px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/330px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/440px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="567" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Countryside near <a href="/wiki/Ngaoundal" title="Ngaoundal">Ngaoundal</a> in Cameroon's <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Region" title="Adamawa Region">Adamawa Region</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An irregular chain of mountains, hills, and plateaus known as the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_line" title="Cameroon line">Cameroon range</a> extends from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a> on the coast—Cameroon's highest point at 4,095 metres (13,435&#160;ft)<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_17_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>—almost to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> at Cameroon's northern border at 13°05'N. This region has a mild climate, particularly on the <a href="/wiki/Western_High_Plateau" title="Western High Plateau">Western High Plateau</a>, although rainfall is high. Its soils are among Cameroon's most fertile, especially around volcanic Mount Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_17_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Volcanism here has created <a href="/wiki/Crater_lake" title="Crater lake">crater lakes</a>. On 21 August 1986, one of these, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nyos" title="Lake Nyos">Lake Nyos</a>, belched carbon dioxide and killed between 1,700 and 2,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> This area has been delineated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund" class="mw-redirect">World Wildlife Fund</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Highlands_forests" title="Cameroonian Highlands forests">Cameroonian Highlands forests</a> ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The southern plateau rises northward to the grassy, rugged <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Plateau" title="Adamawa Plateau">Adamawa Plateau</a>. This feature stretches from the western mountain area and forms a barrier between the country's north and south. Its average elevation is 1,100 metres (3,609&#160;ft),<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_16_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_16-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> and its average temperature ranges from 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F) to 25&#160;°C (77&#160;°F) with high rainfall between April and October peaking in July and August.<sup id="cite_ref-Gwanfogbe_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gwanfogbe-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna" class="mw-redirect">northern lowland region</a> extends from the edge of the Adamawa to Lake Chad with an average elevation of 300 to 350 metres (984 to 1,148&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Neba_17_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Its characteristic vegetation is savanna scrub and grass. This is an arid region with sparse rainfall and high median temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-Green_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameroon has four patterns of drainage. In the south, the principal rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Ntem_River" title="Ntem River" class="mw-redirect">Ntem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nyong_River" title="Nyong River">Nyong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanaga_River" title="Sanaga River">Sanaga</a>, and Wouri. These flow southwestward or westward directly into the Gulf of Guinea. The <a href="/wiki/Dja_River" title="Dja River">Dja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C3%A9%C3%AF_River" title="Kadéï River">Kadéï</a> drain southeastward into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>. In northern Cameroon, the <a href="/wiki/Benue_River" title="Benue River" class="mw-redirect">Bénoué River</a> runs north and west and empties into the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Logon_River" title="Logon River" class="mw-redirect">Logone</a> flows northward into Lake Chad, which Cameroon shares with three neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douala.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Douala.JPG/220px-Douala.JPG" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Douala.JPG/330px-Douala.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Douala.JPG 2x" data-file-width="415" data-file-height="272" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douala.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, the economic capital of Cameroon</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Limbe1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/220px-Limbe1.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/330px-Limbe1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/440px-Limbe1.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
